## COVID - not again, but STILL

Hey all, just your friendly, or not-so friendly, neighborhood ex-ICU nurse here. I'm sure you're all aware that COVID-19
cases has increased a lot in the last two weeks. If not, well, you're now informed. I would like to point out that 
we're not in the third wave. We are still in the FIRST WAVE. Why? Because we never got a handle or control on the outbreak. 
It mostly moved around the country with uncontrolled community spread. To constitute another wave, we would have needed 
to damper the virus nationally like Australia, New Zealand, or South Korea, which we clearly did not. So here we are.

## The dangers of believing in only herd immunity and 99% survival rate

Back in March, people were looking to Sweden regarding their herd immunity approach. Well, it has not worked out well
for them. The number of cases has increased by a factor of five since October. While their numbers don't look anything like 
the United States, it just isn't working out -- spread and infection are happening. According to an October 2020 journal article published in the the 
Journal of the American Medical Association (JAMA) [^1]:

<p style={{padding: '20px', backgroundColor: '#D8d8d8', fontSize: '18px', fontStyle: 'italic', borderRadius: '2em'}}>
Assuming no population immunity and that all individuals are equally susceptible and equally infectious, the herd immunity threshold for SARS-CoV-2 would be expected to range between 50% and 67% in the absence of any interventions.
</p>

Let's talk numbers. This would mean 50%-76% of the population would have to contract the virus somehow.
The world has about 7.8 billion people. The case fatality rate and infection fatality rate of COVID-19 remains to be unknown [^2].
Why? Because this is a novel virus and worldwide testing does not reflect the number of actual cases. Scientists and mathematicians 
can only take an estimate of this number, and the range is wide. So for a very conservative estimate, let's say the overall 
case fatality rate of 1%. That would be 78,000,000 (million) people would die if the entire population was infected with COVID-19. 

Ok, let's say 50% of the population got it for us to be on the low end of herd immunity. 39,000,000 (million) people would die. This 
_99% survival rate_, or 1% case fatality rate, is a dangerous idea to uphold. And if you spout this garbage and want 
to "take your chances," then you're a selfish, soulless, inconsiderate, dung-eating, poop loving fly. I probably won't convince 
you anyway.

![Fly on Head](./images/mike-pence.jpg)

## The vaccine

Yes, the vaccine news is really amazing. I'm not a Debbie downer all the time. I found the news hopeful, refreshing, and 
welcomed. So let's talk about it. The vaccine, or most vaccines even, are still in clinical trials. We are still months, at 
the minimum, from a mass produced vaccine. Distribution is going to be tricky since the vaccine must be kept incredibly cold. 
Logisitically speaking, it's not easy or cheap to haul extremely cold, biological materials. I would have hoped for a sweeping 
federal plan to be in place currently to mobilize and distribute this, but I can't say I have strong faith in that right now.

#### Who needs the vaccine first?

Health care workers, teachers, poorly compensated minimum wage beacons of our society branded as "essential or heroic" workers, 
elderly, inmates, immunocompromised who can receive it, college students, and many others before me. 

#### Who will get it first (probably)?

Rich people, government officials, sports teams, health care workers, teachers, middle class people with insurance, and 
people deemed allies of the United States. I guess I switched back to Debbie downer. But a realistic one.

In short, we're a bit away from competent vaccine coverage. The light is at the end of the tunnel, but we still have to 
weather this storm. 

## It is tiring convincing people to care for others.

Well, _if the prospects of a lockdown severely impacts your life, you're part of the problem_. Yes, I realize some people 
don't have the privilege of staying home and must make a living outside of their houses, putting themselves at risk. But 
if you're going to indoor gatherings, travelling when not necessary, and eating in at restaurants and bars, you should 
just stop. Also, just because your state allows some things doesn't mean it's safe and okay. Examples:
- Outside tents for dining. They have no air circulation. It may distance you slightly from other diners, but there is NO air 
filtration or circulation. It's just an enclosed potential cesspool of virus.
- Going to the gym. I realize this is some people's sanity and ritual. I get it. But part of the recipe for 
COVID-19 infection is exposure time and expelled virus via air or droplet. Gyms are a risk because of the length of time 
and increased respiratory rate.
- Indoor dining with limited capacity. This goes back to exposure time and expelled virus.

A reminder from [Stay In Speak Out](https://stayinspeakout.org):
![Graphic on Exponential Spread](./images/covid--19-transmission-graphic.gif)

## Why would we go into another lockdown if masks work?
Hey bright eyes, not everyone is wearing a mask strictly. What does wearing a mask mean? It means wearing it anytime you're 
outside of your physical house or interacting with someone not in your household. It means having it cover your mouth AND 
nose. It means you're breathing just fine with it on, your CO2 is not building up, and your 
oxygenation is the same, so keep it on.

## But my freedoms
If you make this argument, chances are I won't sway you, and I'm just wasting my words. To quote earlier, "you're a selfish, soulless, inconsiderate, 
dung-eating, poop loving fly." 
![Fly on Head](./images/mike-pence.jpg)

The irony is that freedoms are infringed upon when there is gerrymandering, voter suppression, 
and systemic racism. And people affected by this are most likely the most vulnerable to this pandemic. That's right. Black 
and Brown people are dying in the United States at a higher rate than any other races. Because of systemic racism. So you 
can take your "freedom" to get a skinny Starbucks latte with an AR-15 and shove it.

## I'll just get something flu-like
You don't know that. You could end up on a ventilator. You could not have symptoms. You could die. You could have long-lasting 
health effects like lung scarring or one of the other various reported long hauler effects. You don't know. 

## Health care workers -- show them some respect and decency
Health care workers are supremely tired. And dying on the front lines. The front lines. This term is usually reserved for 
war time. Well, they're in a war with the virus and people who care more about their "freedoms" than other people.

Shown below is an excerpt of a report called Sins of Omission by National Nurses United: [^3]

<p style={{padding: '20px', backgroundColor: '#D8d8d8', fontSize: '18px', fontStyle: 'italic', borderRadius: '2em'}}>
As of Sept. 16, 2020 we found that an estimated 213 registered nurses have died of Covid-19 and related complications and an estimated 1,718 health care
workers, including RNs, have died of Covid-19 and related complications...
Of the 213 registered nurses who have died of Covid-19 and related complications, 124 (58.2 percent) are nurses of color, reflecting the broader
disproportionate impact of Covid-19 on communities of color in the United States.</p>

I hope organizations are supporting their health care workers to the fullest extent. I can feel the exhaustion, the pleads 
for wearing a mask, the cries, the sorrow, and the frustration from health care workers. While I'm not in it and by no means 
know what it's been like in COVID-19, I can feel a fraction of it in my bones. And it hurts so deeply, and I feel like I 
could spit fire.

Remember when we were heralding health care workers? Keep it up. Cheer them on. Support them any way you can. **Often times,
the burden of care goes quietly into the night.**

## End on a prayer
Whoever your maker, creator, or deity is, take a moment with me to send strength, blessings, grace, and peace to 
- Those who have passed
- Those who are grieving
- Those who are recovering
- Those fighting for their lives on a ventilator. Our neighbors, friends, family, colleagues.
- Those working in health care everyday bearing a heavy burden
- Those struggling to make ends meet
- Those who are tired, sad, and anxious
- Those who live on this earth

### Stay home. Save lives. Wear a mask. Get your flu shot [^4].

<p style={{padding: '20px', backgroundColor: '#D8d8d8', fontSize: '18px', fontStyle: 'italic', borderRadius: '2em'}}>
According to BMJ, the risk of death more than doubled in people who also had influenza in addition to COVID-19.
</p>
